 Chapter

  1
Introduction
Define the purpose and scope of the study
     The subject of this report is a 1.4-mile section of the Monticello Road corridor, from Johnson
     Drive to Shawnee Mission Parkway, within the city of Shawnee, Kansas. The limits of the
     study area are shown in Figure 1. A comprehensive study of this corridor was conducted in
     2008-2009 to assess traffic conditions and gather public opinion on options toward improving
     the corridor. The traffic study forecast future traffic volumes and the possible impacts of
     several adjacent roadway projects, some of which would logically impact some travel patterns
     on Monticello Road. Construction plans were developed for improvements, but construction
     was delayed with the major downturn in the local and national economies. The city is now
     planning to proceed with construction, but prior to finalizing scope of construction, has desired
     to review current day traffic conditions within the corridor to assess whether projected traffic
     conditions have been realized, or whether actual traffic conditions differ materially enough to
     warrant changes in the planned scope of improvements to the Monticello Road corridor. This
     amendment to the January 2009 study incorporates new 2012 traffic count data and will
     update the full build-out scenario projections to either confirm or re-assess the improvements
     suggested in the January 2009 study. When the data, analysis, or findings of the January
     2009 study are referenced within this amendment, they will be referred to as having been from
     "previous study".

Recommendations from the 2009 Study
     The previous study developed 14 recommendations for consideration. These
     recommendations were grouped into three priority levels; those recommended for immediate
     implementation, those recommended for a "Phase 2" based on availability of additional
     funding, and those for which the benefit/cost is low enough that implementation is not
     warranted anytime in the near future. Specifically these recommendations and groupings
     were identified as follows:

     Phase 1 (Immediate) Implementation
        1. Install left turn lanes into Clear Creek Elementary School.
                                                                                           th
        2. Install a right turn lane into the north entrance of Mill Valley High School (60 Street).
        3. Widen for two through lanes on southbound Monticello Road at the 61st Street signal.
        4. Re-stripe northbound left turn on Monticello Road at the 61st Street intersection.
        5. Re-stripe southbound Monticello Road at 66th Street to create two through lanes.
            · Since the previous study, this item has already been completed.
        6. Replace curb and gutter and mill and overlay for Monticello Road.
        7. Initiate the Walking School Bus.

     Phase 2 Implementation

           1. Install a traffic signal or roundabout at Monticello Road and Clear Creek Parkway.
           2. Install a right turn lane on eastbound Johnson Drive, turning onto southbound
              Monticello Road.


                                                      1
                                     th
    3. Install a roundabout at 64 Street and Monticello Road.

Not Prioritized for Implementation

    1.   Installing sidewalks east of Monticello Road, north of Johnson Drive.
                                       st
    2.   Installing a roundabout at 61 Street and Monticello Road.
    3.   Overlaying the bridge deck.
                                          th
    4.   Completing the connection of 64 Street through to Woodland Road.

The above recommendations that affect vehicular traffic operations will be reviewed as part of
this traffic study addendum.

Current Traffic Conditions
Define Current (2012) Traffic Conditions and Deficiencies within the
Corridor
      This section of the report will review the current (2012) traffic conditions and analyze those
      volumes to identify any existing deficiencies in traffic operations.

Current Traffic Volumes

      Traffic counts were collected in May 2012 to determine baseline traffic flow conditions. Table 1
      summarizes the intersections and time periods for which counts were taken. The table also
      summarizes the peak periods of traffic flows identified within the count periods. The turning
      movement count data was collected in 15-minute intervals and the full documentation of the
      raw count data is provided in Appendix A for reference.

      The previous study identified the time periods of 7:15­8:15 AM and 3:00-4:00 PM as the peak
      hours of traffic flows through the corridor. These peak periods of traffic flows were observed to
      correspond to the arrival and dismissal periods of the three schools closely spaced within the
      corridor. The peak hour traffic volumes collected in September 2008, and utilized in the
      previous study, are provided in Figure 2 of this addendum for reference purposes. The 2012
      count of current traffic yielded slightly different peak periods, 7:00-8:00 AM and 2:45-3:45 PM.
      It is the traffic volumes from these revised peak periods which will be utilized for the analysis
      contained within this addendum. These 2012 peak hour traffic volumes are summarized in
      Figure 4.




                                                        3
Alignment of Projected vs. Actual Traffic Counts

      The previous study took the 2008 traffic data and developed a near term projection of
      expected traffic volumes within the corridor in year 2010. This projection is summarized in
      Figure 3 of this addendum. This projection was based on several factors, including:
          1. The expected completion of multiple roadway improvements to Silverheel Street and
               Woodsonia Drive, which create an alternate north/south roadway link paralleling the
               Monticello Road corridor to the west.
          2. The expected completion of interchange improvements to Johnson Drive and K-7
               highway.
          3. The construction of a Wal-Mart retail facility at Johnson Drive and K-7 highway.
          4. The continued construction within several housing developments adjacent to the
               Monticello Road corridor.
          5. Continued increase in enrollment at the elementary, middle, and high school facilities
               within the corridor.

      Since the time of the previous study, the roadway improvements anticipated in Items 1 and 2
      above have been completed. These improvements are shown and highlighted in Figure 1.
      The impacts from Items 3-5 above have either not materialized or have not occurred to the
      level anticipated, likely due to downturns in the local and national economies. One of the key
      points of this addendum was that since four years have passed since the original traffic counts,
      the City now has the opportunity to update the traffic counts and replace the projection of 2010
      volumes with a count of known 2012 volumes. Again, a summary of 2012 volumes is shown
      in Figure 4.

      The projected and actual conditions align relatively well. There is always going to be some
      variance in traffic volumes, even those counted on different days of the same week, so any
      variance within +/- 15% should be expected as simply random variance in day-to-day traffic
      flows. For reference, all turning movements are shown in Appendix B. The largest difference
      between projected 2010 and actual 2012 volumes are noted as follows:

          1. A reduction in the eastbound right turns at Johnson Drive and Monticello Road of 90
             vehicles in the AM peak hour. This is likely the result of the roadway extensions of
             Silverheel Street and Woodsonia Drive, which create an alternate north/south route
             paralleling Monticello Road to the west.
          2. A reduction of approximately 100 vehicles in the southbound right turns at Monticello
                           th
             Road and 60 Street during the AM peak hour and a closely corresponding increase
                                                                       st
             in the southbound right turns at Monticello Road and 61 Street. In consultation with
             school officials, there have been no traffic operational changes internal to the middle
             and high school sites which would explain this change in travel patterns.
          3. A consistent increase of 80-100 vehicles during the PM peak hour for the southbound
                                                                          st
             through movement on the portion of the corridor south of 61 Street.
          4. All movements on the westbound approach of Clear Creek Parkway show less than
             projected volumes during both the AM and PM peak periods.
          5. In addition, there are some scattered movements, typically through movements on
             Monticello Road that show variances above or below projected conditions that are
             more than +/- 15%.

      Overall, the projection of year 2010 conditions appears to have reasonably approximated the
      traffic flows which have been subsequently realized. Thus, it is expected that the analysis
      results of this addendum will be closely aligned with the results of the previous study.

      included in Appendix C (without improvements).

      As noted in the previous study, because the Monticello Road corridor has very short peaking
      periods, the operational analysis results should be reviewed in context as they represent the
      operations during the 15-minute portion of the peak hour. Other portions of the peak hour
      should see improved operations, as will all non-peak hours and non-school days.
      The analysis of the peak traffic flows shows that at the intersections of Clear Creek Parkway,
         th              th
      60 Street, and 64 Street, the traffic flows attempting to enter onto Monticello Road, from the
      minor street, are higher than the available in traffic along Monticello Road. More specifically,
      the left turn movements are especially challenged to find the necessary two-way gaps in traffic
      to successfully execute their left turn movement. As previously noted, these delays are


                                                       5
      expected during the heaviest flows of school traffic. During other periods of the day, or on non-
      school days, these delays in entering Monticello Road would not be expected.
      The remaining movements within the corridor were modeled to be currently operating at
      acceptable levels of service.

Operational Analysis of Phase 1 Improvements

      The SYNCHRO inputs were next adjusted to reflect the recommended improvements
      identified in the previous study as Items 1-4 of Phase 1 in order to model the expected traffic
      operations with these improvements in place. Appendix D details the operational analysis of
      current traffic conditions with these recommended improvements in place. The effects on the
      delays and LOS were noted to be very minor and do not address the deficiencies on the of
                                 th              th
      Clear Creek Parkway, 60 Street, and 64 Street approaches noted in Table 2. However, the
      identified roadway improvements do have value in increasing roadway safety and for this
      reason it is still recommended that Items 1, 2 and 4 be implemented as previously
      recommended. These improvements continue to be applicable for the following reasons:
          1. Install left turn lanes into Clear Creek Elementary School. The Monticello Road
             corridor is comprised of only one through lane of travel. Public input from the previous
             study showed a strong desire to maintain, if possible, the two through lanes instead of
             widening to four through lanes. A major constraint to traffic flows on two-lane
             roadways is vehicles stopped in traffic to execute a left turn movement. These
             vehicles cause delay for all following vehicles and represent a safety hazard due to
             the speed differential between slowing or stopped vehicles turning left and through
             traffic wishing to maintain their running speed. The left turn movement at all public
                                                 th
             street intersections other than 56 Street, which has only 1-3 left turn movements
             during the subject peak hours, have auxiliary left turn lanes established to allow left
             turn vehicles to decelerate and queue outside of the through lanes of traffic. The
                                                                                                     nd
             remaining areas where auxiliary left turn lanes do not exist are northbound at 62
             street (very low turning volumes of 0-3 vehicles per hour), southbound at Sacred
             Heart Church (two driveways, one with significant left turn volumes and one with
             nearly no left turn movements), and southbound at Clear Creek Elementary School.
             The school has one driveway with significant left turn movements, 33 in the AM peak
             hour and 39 in the PM peak hour. This area of the corridor also facilitates some
             widening in that there is additional offset spacing from the roadway corridor to the first
             adjacent residential lots. The establishment of left turn lanes will improve the safety of
             these movements and as a result, should continue to receive strong consideration for
             inclusion in the planned improvements. It would further reduce the number of
             remaining left turn occurrences from Monticello Road which are not protected with
             auxiliary lanes.
          2. Install a southbound right turn lane into the north entrance of Mill Valley High
                           th
             School (60 Street).          While the implementation of this improvement does not
             significantly improve delays experienced by southbound traffic, it does, for reasons
             similar to those stated previously; improve the safety for those executing the
             movement. The traffic counts yield an AM peak hour volume of 293 vehicles making
             this movement, which satisfy any widely accepted access management guideline for
             the addition of a right turn auxiliary lane. It is recommended the addition of the
             auxiliary right turn lane remain in the scope of improvements for Monticello Road.
                                                                                              st
          3. Widen for two through lanes on southbound Monticello Road at the 61 Street
             signal. The AM peak hour volumes provide difficulty in assigning right-of-way splits in
             the signal timing to adequately service each movement and minimize delays and
             queuing. Specifically, the combinations of high northbound left turning movements,
             high southbound movements, and high eastbound exiting movements all are
             competing for available signal timing.        The previous study provided the


                                                        6
                                                                                              st
              recommendation of developing two southbound through lanes approaching 61 Street
                                    nd
              and extending to 62 Street. This would allow southbound traffic to queue in multiple
              lanes and will reduce the signal timing required to service the southbound movement,
              thereby freeing up this time to be reallocated to other movements. An alternate
              approach would be to develop a dual left turn lane for the northbound left turns into
                                                                                                     st
              the school site. This would require similar widening on Monticello Road between 61
                      nd
              and 62 Street and would also require adjustment of the school driveway to accept
              the dual inbound movement. The school driveway currently widens to accommodate
              two lanes of traffic approximately 150 feet internal to the site. The driveway would
              need to be modified to extend the acceptance of two lanes to the Monticello Road
              intersection. This option was modeled through a SYNCHRO analysis and resulted in
              significantly improved operations for the signal and reduction in northbound queue
              spill over. This alternate recommendation will be discussed further in Chapter 3 for full
              build-out traffic conditions.
              It is also noted the existing signal timing includes unusually long red clearance timings
              of 3.9 to 4.3 seconds on the side street movements. It is unknown the reasons
              behind these timings being implemented (assumed to be crash experience or some
              other safety-related reason) but these timings do effectively degrade the signal
              operations by reducing the total effective green time for movement of traffic. The
              previous study also identified a roundabout as a possible improvement at this
              intersection, although it was categorized as a low priority. The existing traffic signal
              has the benefit of controlling crosswalks that have significant use by school
              pedestrians during the peak hours. With the improvements in operations achieved
              with the dual northbound left turn lane concept, and the benefit to pedestrians of the
              traffic signal, it is no longer recommended that a roundabout be considered at this
              intersection.
                                                                                st
          4. Re-stripe northbound left turn on Monticello Road at the 61 Street intersection.
             This recommendation does not involve the widening of Monticello Road or the
             introduction of a new auxiliary lane, but simply involves re-striping of the available
                                                                                       nd
             width to shift some of the queue storage length from southbound 62 Street to
                              st
             northbound 61 Street. This recommendation continues to appear prudent based on
             current traffic volumes. The current counts show 245 vehicles making the northbound
             left turn at 61st Street during the AM peak hour while only one vehicle is making the
                                          nd
             southbound left turn at 62 Street. A minimum storage length of 50 feet should be
                                                            nd
             reserved for the southbound movement at 62 , along with an appropriate length of
             taper, but the remaining storage length, approximately 30 feet, can be reallocated to
                                                     st
             the northbound left turn storage for 61 Street. As stated immediately above in Item
             3, an alternate improvement recommendation that has been identified is the
             implementation of a dual northbound left turn lane into the school. This is discussed
             more in Chapter 3 for full build-out conditions. If a dual lane is implemented, it is
             continued to be recommended that the dual lane be made as long as possible and
             incorporate any available distance not necessary for the queuing of vehicles for the
                                        nd
             southbound left turn at 62 Street.

Operational Analysis of Phase 2 Improvements

      As previously noted, the analysis of the peak traffic flows shows that at the intersections of
                                 th                 th
      Clear Creek Parkway, 60 Street, and 64 Street, the traffic flows attempting to enter onto
      Monticello Road, from the minor street, are higher than the available in traffic along Monticello
      Road. This results in these movements experiencing a failed level of service, indicating
      average delays exceeding 50 seconds per vehicle. This is similar to the findings of the
      previous study that resulted in identifying possible Phase 2 improvements that included a traffic
                                                               th
      signal or roundabout at Clear Creek Parkway and at 64 Street.



                                                       7
Interim Striping
A possible interim improvement not identified in the previous study is the striping of designated
                      th                         nd                                           th
left-turn lanes at 60 Street (westbound), 62 Street (eastbound and westbound), 64 Street
                                         th
(eastbound and westbound), and 64 Terrace (eastbound). Currently there is no striping on
these approaches, although they have the width available to for dual lanes and field
observation indicates that traffic is indeed utilizing the available width to form two approach
lanes on these side streets. Providing a distinct separation of the movements should improve
the level of service for the right turning portion of the approach traffic, in that it would no longer
be subject to delays of left turning traffic. The model inputs for the current year traffic model
were adjusted to simulate dual lanes on these approaches and model outputs analyzed to
determine the level of improvement. Unfortunately, while there was some improvement in
average delays for the side street approaches, this improvement proved to be relatively minor,
typically only a few seconds per vehicle in decreased delay, and did not resolve the modeled
failed level of service conditions during the peak hours. Detailed output for this analysis is
contained in Appendix E.

Traffic Signals
Traffic volumes were collected for 2012 for eleven hours at the intersections of Clear Creek
                     th
Parkway and at 64 Street. This level of data collection allows for evaluation of each of the
volume related traffic signal warrants contained in the Manual on Uniform Traffic Control
Devices. Summaries of this warrant analysis are provided in Appendix F. The findings are
that while traffic volumes are high enough to meet portions of various traffic signal warrants,
there would need to be a considerable increase in traffic volumes in order to meet the
thresholds required to fully satisfy signal warrants. Thus, based on traffic volumes and review
of applicable traffic signal warrants, the installation of traffic signals is not found to be
warranted.

Roundabout
Currently, since Monticello Road is a two-lane facility with no center median, left turns
from side streets need to be completed in one movement. The reason for the failed level
of service is simply there are not enough simultaneous gaps in both directions of
Monticello Road traffic to accommodate the left turn demand from these two streets. An
improvement which would address this problem is the installation of roundabouts. These
were identified in the original 2009 traffic study as a possible Phase 2 improvement.
Roundabouts would eliminate the left turn movement and the corresponding need for
simultaneous gaps in Monticello Road traffic. Left turns would be accomplished by
initially turning right, using one-direction gaps in traffic, and following the roundabout to
complete the movement. Table 3 (without additional improvements) summarizes the
delay and corresponding level of service at the subject intersection for both AM & PM
peak hour conditions under roundabout control. A detailed printout of the operational
analysis is included in Appendix G.

to 7.3s, which improves the LOS D to a LOS A.

Eastbound Right Turn Lane at Johnson Drive
Another Phase 2 recommendation of the previous study was the construction of an auxiliary
right turn lane for the east to southbound right turn movement at Monticello Road and Johnson
Drive. The 2008 turning volume was 173 vehicles in the AM peak hour and was projected to
increase to 181 by year 2010. The updated counts, taken in 2012, showed a decrease in this
movement to 90 vehicles during the AM peak hour. A possible explanation for this is the
recent roadway extensions of Silverheel Street and Woodsonia Drive, which create an
alternate north/south travel option which parallels Monticello Road to the west. Some drivers
may be utilizing this alternate route and turning right off of Johnson Drive prior to Monticello
Road. The recommendation for an auxiliary lane in the previous study was based on general
safety factors similar to those described earlier for other proposed improvements. The number
of eastbound right turns would satisfy any generally accepted access management guidelines
for warranting construction of a right turn lane. The previous study grouped the improvement
as a Phase 2 priority based on field observations of traffic and the fact the improvement would
yield relatively little improvement in travels times or delays. The current traffic volumes would
lessen the safety issue and further reduce the urgency of implementing this improvement.
However, it is expected that with additional growth, the right turn traffic volumes will rebound
and this will be discussed further in Chapter 3.



                                                  9
 Chapter

   3
Full Build-Out Traffic Conditions
Define Anticipated Traffic Conditions at Full Development of the
Study Area
      This section of the report will discuss the projected traffic volumes traveling within the corridor
      at the time the entire study area is fully developed, which for purposes of this study is assumed
      to be year 2020.

Projected Background Traffic

      By the time the study area is at full build-out, it is anticipated there will be several
      improvements made and developments that occur outside the study area in western Shawnee
      that will affect traffic traveling on Monticello Road. It is anticipated that there will be additional
      through movements along Monticello Road that are generated from travel with origins and
      destinations outside of the Study Area. The previous study estimated an additional 3,000
                                                             th
      vehicles per day on Monticello Road between 66 Street and Johnson Drive due to these
      influences increasing through volumes. These assumptions regarding increases in
      background through traffic are still judged to be appropriate.

Projecting 2012 Traffic Counts to Full Build-Out (2020) Traffic Volumes

      The methodologies and assumptions utilized in the previous study for projecting future
      volumes based on growth expected within the study area were reviewed and judged to remain
      valid and applicable. Some of the expected development has not yet occurred, which simply
      means the full value of the expected trip increases need to be added to the current (year 2012)
      volumes in order to estimate the full build-out conditions. Using the methodologies and
      assumptions utilized in the previous study, and accounting for the levels of assumed
      development having actually occurred by 2012, an updated projection of full build-out traffic
      conditions was developed and is summarized in Figure 5. A detailed summary of the
      calculations is provided in Appendix H.

      As noted in the previous study, because the Monticello Road corridor has very short peaking
      periods, the operational analysis results should be reviewed in context as they represent the
      operations during the 15-minute portion of the peak hour. Other portions of the peak hour
      should see improved operations, as will all non-peak hours and non-school days. Most of the
      issues regarding failed levels of service for full build-out conditions are the same as those
      identified for current year, 2012, conditions. Thus the recommendations contained in the
      previous study will first be evaluated and discussed for their continued application.

Operational Analysis of Phase 1 Improvements
      Appendix J details the operational analysis of the full build-out conditions with improvement
      recommendations identified in the previous study as Items 1-4 of Phase 1. The following
      recommendations are made regarding these identified improvement alternatives:




                                                     11
      1. Install left turn lanes into Clear Creek Elementary School. For the safety reasons
         stated previously in Chapter 2, this recommendation remains valid, even though the effect
         in improving travel times and reducing average delays is relatively minor.
                                                                                              th
      2. Install a right turn lane into the north entrance of Mill Valley High School (60
         Street). For the safety reason stated previously in Chapter 2, this recommendation
         remains valid, even though the effect in improving travel times and reducing delays is
         relatively minor.
      3. Widen for two through lanes on southbound Monticello Road at the 61st Street
         signal. As was discussed in Chapter 2, the signalized intersection of Monticello Road and
            st
         61 Street currently experiences high northbound queuing, which extends beyond the
         limits of the current auxiliary lane and blocks the northbound through lane during portions
         of the AM peak hour. In addition, some of the approaches operate currently under a failed
         level of service that will only worsen with full build-out traffic flows. The previous study
                                                                                             st
         suggested developing two southbound through lanes from the approach to 61 Street
                      nd
         through 62 Street as a means of increasing capacity through the intersection. This
         increased capacity would allow some reallocation of signal timing splits to address the
         northbound queuing issue. Field observation of 2012 traffic flows in the AM peak hour
         revealed there are several signal cycles where the northbound left turn queue significantly
         exceeds the available capacity. The spillover effects create a queuing issue that extends
         nearly 800 feet south of the intersection. An alternate improvement recommendation is to
         develop auxiliary lanes for dual northbound left turns into the school. Modeling this
         improvement through SYNCHRO showed that for full build-out conditions, all approaches
         to the signal could operate at a level of service D or better during both the AM and
         afternoon peak periods. The only approach operating as low as a D is the eastbound
         approach, exiting the schools, during the afternoon peak period. All other approaches
         during both the AM and afternoon peak periods were modeled to operate at a level of
         service C or better. The vehicle queues were modeled to be only 60% of their previous
         length, which should allow for full storage to be made within the dual auxiliary lanes,
         thereby eliminating the spillover problem affecting northbound through movements.
      4. Re-stripe northbound left turn on Monticello Road at the 61st Street intersection.
         This recommendation remains valid for the reasons previously stated under Chapter 2 of
         this addendum. If the dual northbound left turn lane recommendation is implemented at
         this intersection, the dual lanes should still be developed and striped to make use of as
                                                                st             nd
         much of the storage space as possible between 61 Street and 62 Street.

Operational Analysis of Phase 2 Improvements
      As previously noted, the analysis of the peak traffic flows shows that at the intersections of
                                   th                th
      Clear Creek Parkway, 60 Street, and 64 Street, the traffic flows attempting to enter onto
      Monticello Road, from the minor street, are higher than the available in traffic along Monticello
      Road. This results in these movements experiencing a failed level of service, indicating
      average delays exceeding 50 seconds per vehicle. This situation is only expected to increase
      in severity for full build-out traffic volumes, unless some modification is identified to improve
      traffic operations.

      Interim Striping
      In Chapter 2, for current traffic volumes, the concept of providing interim striping as a means of
      clearly delineating two lanes on each approach to Monticello Road, could improve operations
      by providing separation of the most challenged movement, the left turns onto Monticello Road.
      While this improvement does provide some improvement in operations, the improvement is
      very slight. A detailed summary of the analysis is contained in Appendix K. In addition, field
      observation indicates that traffic is already operating under this assumption, despite the lack of
      pavement markings. So, while there is minimal cost to implement this recommendation, there


                                                       12
  is also minimal impact from making this change. To better address the operational problems,
  other modifications should be identified, if possible.

  Traffic Signals
  Full build-out traffic volumes were reviewed for the intersections of Clear Creek Parkway and
        th
  at 64 Street. The findings are that while traffic volumes are expected to increase within the
  corridor at full build-out, the volumes will still not be high enough to meet signal warrants.
  Thus, based on traffic volumes and review of applicable traffic signal warrants, the installation
  of traffic signals is not found to be warranted.

  Roundabout
  The option of a roundabout at several intersections was discussed in Chapter 2. This concept
  was further reviewed for full build-out traffic flows. The results of this analysis are shown in
  Table 5 and a detailed summary of the analysis is contained in Appendix L.

With the installation of roundabouts, the side street delays are significantly reduced. Delay is,
however, transferred to the north/south through movements that now need to navigate the
roundabout. Overall, all movements at all intersections are modeled to operate at level of service
D or better for full build-out traffic flows. Due to the close spacing of intersections through the
                                               st
corridor and the presence of signals at 61 Street, the installation of roundabouts at each of the
four intersections noted above is not realistic. Due to current and projected side street volumes,
the intersections prioritized for consideration of roundabouts is first the intersection at Clear
                                                       th
Creek Parkway and second the intersection at 64 Street. For further reasons discussed in
                                                                       th               nd
Chapter 4 the installation of roundabouts at the intersections of 60 Street and 62 Street are
not recommended.


                                                   13
Chapter

 4
Recommendations
          The previous study grouped recommendations into three broad categories of prioritization.
          However, since the previous study, the timing of Phase 1 construction has been delayed
          for four years. Based on recent discussions with members of the Shawnee Public Works
          staff, there is now a desire to group all improvements that are necessary to accommodate
          full-build out traffic conditions into a single project. Thus, if an improvement is necessary
          for traffic safety or efficient traffic flows under expected full build-out traffic volumes, it
          should be identified so that an appropriate scope of improvements can be developed and
          funding secured. The remainder of this section will document the major points along the
          corridor, starting from the north and moving south, and what recommendations, if any,
          there are for improvements.

    Johnson Drive
          The previous study provided a Phase 2 recommendation of adding an eastbound right
          turn lane at this intersection. This recommendation is primarily fueled by the high number
          of right turns (173 in year 2008) executed in the AM peak hour. However, the 2012 traffic
          count now shows a nearly 50% drop in this volume to 90 vehicles. With full development
          in the area, the right turn volume is expected to rebound to approximately 153 vehicles in
          the AM peak hour. The analysis of current and future traffic volumes show acceptable
          levels of service for the existing lane geometrics at the intersection. The acceptable level
          of service in year 2020 is achieved using the same signal phasing, but a modified timing
          split of the available phasing. As with any traffic signal maintained by the city, the volumes
          and timings for this signal should be reviewed on a programmed basis, at least once every
          five years, to ensure the signal timings are appropriate for the current volumes. Based on
          existing and future year expected volumes, the right turn volume is high enough to satisfy
          generally accepted warrants contained in many access management guidelines.
          Recommendation: Construction of an eastbound right turn auxiliary lane is
          recommended, but this would be a lower priority than other improvements.

    Sacred Heart Church Driveways
          This church has two driveways, the north being signed as an entrance and the south drive
          being signed as an exit. However, the school's web site directs motorists to utilize the
          north drive as both the entrance and exit. As traffic counts show, the majority of the
          entering and exiting movements do indeed utilize the north driveway. The south driveway
          experiences very low traffic volumes (11-20 total vehicles during the AM and afternoon
          peak hours). The north driveway experiences volumes of 52-107 total vehicles during the
          AM and afternoon peak hours. The north driveway is located in an undesirable location in
          that it is located in conflict with the storage bay for the northbound left turn movement at
          Johnson Drive. Therefore, vehicles turning left into or out of the north driveway need to
          cross the left turn queue, when present, to execute the movement. This is undesirable
          from a safety standpoint. A possible improvement would be to extend the 3-lane section
          of Monticello Road approximately 300 feet to the south, creating a southbound left turn
          lane into the south church driveway. This driveway could then be used for left turns in and


                                                        14
   out of the site, while the north driveway could be limited, by driveway restriction or by
   center raised median to serve only right turn in and right turns out. This would allow the
   left turns into the church site to be made from a protected auxiliary lane and would
   separate these movements from the left turn storage queues at Johnson Drive. The
   impact of the change in traffic patterns would need to be discussed with church leaders,
   but this proposed change would not appear to adversely affect travel times or travel
   patterns to any significant degree.
   Recommendation: Extend the current 3-lane section approximately 300 additional feet
   south of Johnson Drive in order to create an auxiliary left turn lane into the south driveway
   of the Sacred Heart Church. Then add signage to the north driveway in order to limit the
   movements at the north driveway to right turns in and right turns out.

56th Street
   Traffic volumes at this public street intersection are relatively light (25-28) total vehicles in
   the AM and afternoon peak periods. Like other intersections within the corridor, the
   movement with the highest delay is the left turn movement entering Monticello Road.
   However, the LOS was modeled as a "D" during the peak hours of full-build out traffic.
   This level of operation is deemed acceptable and there are no recommendations for
   improvement at this intersection.
   Recommendation: None

Clear Creek Parkway
   This intersection has one of the highest side street approach volumes within the corridor.
   This is not surprising, since Clear Creek Parkway extends west to the new frontage roads
   and bridge over K-7 and extends east to Woodland Drive. Thus the parkway serves as a
   significant connection within the roadway network of the study area. The left turns onto
   Monticello Road are particularly challenged during the AM and afternoon peaks, with failed
   levels of service and significant delays. Striping the approaches to clearly define two lanes
   of traffic were modeled to result in small improvements in total side street delays, but the
   left turn movements continue to operate with a failed level of service. Traffic signal
   warrants were reviewed, but the combination of major street and minor street traffic
   volumes was not expected to be enough, even under full build-out conditions, to meet
   applicable traffic signal warrants. The volumes in the peak hour are not high enough to
   meet the peaking warrants and the volumes during the non-peak periods are not high
   enough to meet any of the 8-hour traffic warrants. Finally, a roundabout was reviewed as
   a means of eliminating the need for executing a left turn and channeling all movements
   into an initial right turn entry into the roundabout. The roundabout concept was shown to
   improve the level of service for the side street movements, to some detriment of the
   through movements. All approaches were modeled to operate at a level of service D or
   better during both the AM and afternoon peak periods.
   Recommendation: Based on the key connection this intersection forms for the street
   network within the study area, it is recommended that improvement be made to enhance
   the peak hour traffic operations. The installation of a roundabout is recommended as the
   appropriate improvement to consider. The roundabout will need to be driven by all traffic
   moving along the Monticello Road corridor. During non-peak hours, while this may be less
   desirable for through movements, the average delay for the through movements should
   be negligible. By eliminating the need to seek simultaneous gaps in Monticello Road
   traffic, the side street movements will be much improved during the peak hour periods.




                                                  15
Clear Creek Elementary School Driveways
   The two driveways experience a moderate number of southbound left turns (20-42 left
   turns each) during the AM and afternoon peak hour periods. These left turns are currently
   executed out of the southbound through lane of traffic, because there are no auxiliary
   lanes for these movements. The level of service calculations for current and full build-out
   traffic does not indicate this significantly affects delays for southbound through vehicles.
   However for safety reasons discussed previously in this addendum, it is recommended
   that auxiliary lanes be installed to separate these left turns from the southbound through
   movements. The exiting left turn movements at the driveways operate under a failed level
   of service in the AM and afternoon peak hours. However, the expected queue lengths are
   only two vehicles or less. Thus, while exiting vehicles can expect average delays of over
   50 seconds, there are relatively few vehicles experiencing this delay at any one time.
   Thus, no recommendations are deemed to be justified.
   Recommendation: Widen Monticello Road in this area to a 3-lane section in order to
   develop southbound left turn auxiliary lanes into each school driveway.

60th Street
     th
   60 Street has a public street approach on the east and a high school access on the west.
   There is an extremely high southbound right turn volume (293 counted in year 2012) in the
   AM peak hour. This volume would meet the thresholds of any generally accepted access
   management guideline for the installation of an auxiliary right turn lane. Operationally, this
   intersection experiences a failed level of service, in full-build out conditions, for the
   westbound approach in the AM peak hour and both the east and westbound approaches
   in the afternoon peak hour. The most significant problems occur on the westbound
   approach (traffic heading toward the school) during the AM peak hour and on the
   eastbound approach (traffic exiting the school) in the afternoon peak hour. During field
   observation of current year, 2012 traffic volumes, it was identified that a number of the
   east/west trips through this intersection originate on Clear Creek Parkway, east of Lone
                                                        th
   Elm Street. The use of Lone Elm Street and 60 Street are obviously viewed by some
   motorists as a shorter distance and/or shorter travel time, especially if traffic flows are
   similarly congested at Monticello Road and Clear Creek Parkway. With improvement to
   Clear Creek Parkway with the installation of a roundabout, more of these motorists may, in
   the future, be inclined to remain on Clear Creek Parkway and access Monticello Road
   though the roundabout. This reduction in traffic would reduce the delays for the remaining
   vehicles on the east and westbound approaches. Otherwise, the improvement at this
   intersection will likely need to be in the form of a roundabout if the goal is to improve the
   side street delays during the peak hour. However, given the short spacing of this
   intersection to a proposed roundabout at Clear Creek Parkway to the north and a signal at
      st
   61 Street to the south, it is not recommended that an additional roundabout be added at
      th
   60 Street.
   Recommendation: Add a southbound right turn lane into the school. The lane should
   have a full width for a minimum of 100 feet, up to 200 feet if possible, and appropriate
   entrance taper. The full width will allow for vehicles planning to turn right to queue
   momentary while they wait for school pedestrians to cross the driveway outside of the
   through lane of southbound traffic. The City should resist further changes in traffic control
   and seek to invest in improvements at Clear Creek Parkway, which could have some
                          th
   residual benefits at 60 Street by diverting some trips.




                                                16
61st Street
     St
   61 Street is a signalized intersection which is a major focal point for both vehicular and
   pedestrian ingress and egress to the schools. During the peak portions of the peak hours
   of school arrival and dismissal, the allocation of available green time, along with the
   capacities of the current lane configurations, result in failed levels of service on several
   approaches and an extremely long northbound left turn queue that spillover into the
   adjoining through lane for northbound traffic. Some geometric improvement is needed to
   increase the capacity through the intersection. The previous study recommended
                                                                          st                 nd
   developing dual southbound through lanes from the approach to 61 Street through 62
   Street. Further evaluation has focused on the development of a dual left turn auxiliary
   lane to accommodate left turns into the school. This concept was modeled and shown to
   address the queuing and spillover problems for the northbound approach. The dual left
   turn also allowed for the reallocation of some signal timing which improved the level of
   service for all approaches to a level of service D or better during the AM and afternoon
   peak periods. For detailed analysis, see Appendix E (2012) and Appendix K (Full Build-
   Out).
   Recommendation: Create dual northbound left turn lane of maximum length, as allowed
                                                     nd
   by shortening the southbound left turn lane at 62 Street. This will require modification of
   both the entering and exiting lanes of the school driveway for 115 feet (measured from the
   stop bar). As part of the signal modifications, the signal timing plan should be reviewed,
   along with the current clearance times to optimize the timing for the adjusted traffic flows.

62nd Street
   This street serves a limited number of homes, and as a result currently has relatively low
   traffic volumes (25-28 total vehicles) in the AM and afternoon peak hours. While the left
   turns will, like other intersections along the corridor, experience challenges in finding an
   adequate number of gaps, the low number of vehicles affected by these delays would not
   warrant improvements.
   Recommendations: None

64th Street
   The characteristics and issues at this intersection closely parallel those of Clear Creek
                   th
   Parkway. 64 Street provides a direct connection to the Woodsonia Drive/K-7 Frontage
   Road to the west and extending east approximately one-half mile, although it does not
   provide connection to Woodland Drive (see Figure 1). During the AM and afternoon peak
   hour periods, the side street approaches operate with a failed level of service. The largest
   contributors to the delays are those experienced by the left turn movements, which need
   to wait for a simultaneous gap in north and southbound traffic in order to complete the left
   turn in a single movement. Striping the east and westbound approaches to clearly define
   two lanes of travel approaching the intersection and separate the left turns from the other
   movements, would be expected to provide some reduction in delays, but the left turns will
   continue to operate at a failed level of service. This was modeled to be especially
   problematic for the westbound left turns in the AM peak hour, due to the relatively high
   volume (85 vehicles). Traffic signal warrants were reviewed and the volumes for both
   current and full-development traffic are not expected to meet any applicable traffic signal
   warrants. Field observation of this intersection during the peak hours indicate that
   motorists routinely accept gaps in traffic, to execute their turning movements, that are less
   than standard gap acceptance utilized in traffic models. Thus, while the models indicate a
   fail level of service, actual field observation would indicate that actual delays do not reach
   failed level of service and the side street queuing is limited to only about 2 vehicles. This
   is significantly less than the queue on Clear Creek Parkway. Thus, while a roundabout


                                                17
would improve side street delays, the importance of addressing these delays is judged to
be less of a priority than at Clear Creek Parkway. If the city was able to budget funds for a
roundabout, it would serve as a good traffic calming entry to the school portion of the
                                                                st
corridor. The traffic signal at the main school entrance at 61 Street would be bracketed,
both to the north and the south, by roundabouts spaced approximately 2000 feet in
advance of the signal. This would provide a good balance of traffic calming and traffic
control features, without cluttering the corridor with an over-proliferation of roundabouts or
similar traffic control features.

Recommendation: If budget allows, it is recommended that a roundabout be constructed
at this intersection. If budget allows for the construction of only one roundabout in the
                                                                             th
corridor, it is recommended that Clear Creek Parkway be prioritized over 64 Street and
        th
that 64 Street remain in its current configuration.
